            <meta name="dc.title" content="First draft genome assembly of the Argane tree&amp;nbsp;(&lt;i&gt;Argania spinosa&lt;/i&gt;)">
            <meta name="dc.description" content=" Background: The Argane tree ( Argania spinosa L. Skeels) is an endemic tree of mid-western Morocco that plays an important socioeconomic and ecologic role for a dense human population in an arid zone. Several studies confirmed the importance of this species as a food and feed source and as a resource for both pharmaceutical and cosmetic compounds. Unfortunately, the argane tree ecosystem is facing significant threats from environmental changes (global warming, over-population) and over-exploitation. Limited research has been conducted, however, on argane tree genetics and genomics, which hinders its conservation and genetic improvement. 
 Methods: Here, we present a draft genome assembly of A. spinosa . A reliable reference genome of&amp;nbsp; A. spinosa &amp;nbsp;was created using a hybrid&amp;nbsp; de novo assembly approach combining short and long sequencing reads. 
 Results: In total, 144 Gb Illumina HiSeq reads and 7.6 Gb PacBio reads were produced and assembled. The final draft genome comprises 75 327 scaffolds totaling 671 Mb with an N50 of 49 916 kb. The draft assembly is close to the genome size estimated by k -mers distribution and covers 89% of complete and 4.3 % of partial Arabidopsis orthologous groups in BUSCO. 
 Conclusion: The A. spinosa genome will be useful for assessing biodiversity leading to efficient conservation of this endangered endemic tree. Furthermore, the genome may enable genome-assisted cultivar breeding, and provide a better understanding of important metabolic pathways and their underlying genes for both cosmetic and pharmacological.">

            <meta name="citation_title" content="First draft genome assembly of the Argane tree&amp;nbsp;(&lt;i&gt;Argania spinosa&lt;/i&gt;)">
            <meta name="citation_abstract" content=" Background: The Argane tree ( Argania spinosa L. Skeels) is an endemic tree of mid-western Morocco that plays an important socioeconomic and ecologic role for a dense human population in an arid zone. Several studies confirmed the importance of this species as a food and feed source and as a resource for both pharmaceutical and cosmetic compounds. Unfortunately, the argane tree ecosystem is facing significant threats from environmental changes (global warming, over-population) and over-exploitation. Limited research has been conducted, however, on argane tree genetics and genomics, which hinders its conservation and genetic improvement. 
 Methods: Here, we present a draft genome assembly of A. spinosa . A reliable reference genome of&amp;nbsp; A. spinosa &amp;nbsp;was created using a hybrid&amp;nbsp; de novo assembly approach combining short and long sequencing reads. 
 Results: In total, 144 Gb Illumina HiSeq reads and 7.6 Gb PacBio reads were produced and assembled. The final draft genome comprises 75 327 scaffolds totaling 671 Mb with an N50 of 49 916 kb. The draft assembly is close to the genome size estimated by k -mers distribution and covers 89% of complete and 4.3 % of partial Arabidopsis orthologous groups in BUSCO. 
 Conclusion: The A. spinosa genome will be useful for assessing biodiversity leading to efficient conservation of this endangered endemic tree. Furthermore, the genome may enable genome-assisted cultivar breeding, and provide a better understanding of important metabolic pathways and their underlying genes for both cosmetic and pharmacological.">
            <meta name="citation_description" content=" Background: The Argane tree ( Argania spinosa L. Skeels) is an endemic tree of mid-western Morocco that plays an important socioeconomic and ecologic role for a dense human population in an arid zone. Several studies confirmed the importance of this species as a food and feed source and as a resource for both pharmaceutical and cosmetic compounds. Unfortunately, the argane tree ecosystem is facing significant threats from environmental changes (global warming, over-population) and over-exploitation. Limited research has been conducted, however, on argane tree genetics and genomics, which hinders its conservation and genetic improvement. 
 Methods: Here, we present a draft genome assembly of A. spinosa . A reliable reference genome of&amp;nbsp; A. spinosa &amp;nbsp;was created using a hybrid&amp;nbsp; de novo assembly approach combining short and long sequencing reads. 
 Results: In total, 144 Gb Illumina HiSeq reads and 7.6 Gb PacBio reads were produced and assembled. The final draft genome comprises 75 327 scaffolds totaling 671 Mb with an N50 of 49 916 kb. The draft assembly is close to the genome size estimated by k -mers distribution and covers 89% of complete and 4.3 % of partial Arabidopsis orthologous groups in BUSCO. 
 Conclusion: The A. spinosa genome will be useful for assessing biodiversity leading to efficient conservation of this endangered endemic tree. Furthermore, the genome may enable genome-assisted cultivar breeding, and provide a better understanding of important metabolic pathways and their underlying genes for both cosmetic and pharmacological.">

  "description": "Background: The Argane tree ( Argania spinosa L. Skeels) is an endemic tree of mid-western Morocco that plays an important socioeconomic and ecologic role for a dense human population in an arid zone. Several studies confirmed the importance of this species as a food and feed source and as a resource for both pharmaceutical and cosmetic compounds. Unfortunately, the argane tree ecosystem is facing significant threats from environmental changes (global warming, over-population) and over-exploitation. Limited research has been conducted, however, on argane tree genetics and genomics, which hinders its conservation and genetic improvement.
Methods: Here, we present a draft genome assembly of A. spinosa. A reliable reference genome of  A. spinosa was created using a hybrid  de novo assembly approach combining short and long sequencing reads.
Results: In total, 144 Gb Illumina HiSeq reads and 7.6 Gb PacBio reads were produced and assembled. The final draft genome comprises 75 327 scaffolds totaling 671 Mb with an N50 of 49 916 kb. The draft assembly is close to the genome size estimated by k-mers distribution and covers 89% of complete and 4.3 % of partial Arabidopsis orthologous groups in BUSCO.
Conclusion: The A. spinosa genome will be useful for assessing biodiversity leading to efficient conservation of this endangered endemic tree. Furthermore, the genome may enable genome-assisted cultivar breeding, and provide a better understanding of important metabolic pathways and their underlying genes for both cosmetic and pharmacological."
}

id=anchor-abstract> <h2 class="article-headings article-page-abstract"> <span class="f1r-article-mobile-inline abstract-heading-border"></span> <span class=js-article-abstract-title>Abstract</span> </h2> <div class="article-abstract article-page-general-text-mobile research-layout"> <div class="abstract-text is-expanded js-article-abstract"> <b>Background: </b>The Argane tree ( <i>Argania spinosa </i>L. Skeels) is an endemic tree of mid-western Morocco that plays an important socioeconomic and ecologic role for a dense human population in an arid zone. Several studies confirmed the importance of this species as a food and feed source and as a resource for both pharmaceutical and cosmetic compounds. Unfortunately, the argane tree ecosystem is facing significant threats from environmental changes (global warming, over-population) and over-exploitation. Limited research has been conducted, however, on argane tree genetics and genomics, which hinders its conservation and genetic improvement.<br/> <b>Methods: </b>Here, we present a draft genome assembly of <i>A. spinosa</i>. A reliable reference genome of&nbsp; <i>A. spinosa</i>&nbsp;was created using a hybrid&nbsp; <i>de novo</i> assembly approach combining short and long sequencing reads.<br/> <b>Results: </b>In total, 144 Gb Illumina HiSeq reads and 7.6 Gb PacBio reads were produced and assembled. The final draft genome comprises 75 327 scaffolds totaling 671 Mb with an N50 of 49 916 kb. The draft assembly is close to the genome size estimated by <i>k</i>-mers distribution and covers 89% of complete and 4.3 % of partial <i>Arabidopsis</i> orthologous groups in BUSCO.<br/> <b>Conclusion: </b>The <i>A. spinosa</i> genome will be useful for assessing biodiversity leading to efficient conservation of this endangered endemic tree. Furthermore, the genome may enable genome-assisted cultivar breeding, and provide a better understanding of important metabolic pathways and their underlying genes for both cosmetic and pharmacological. </div> <div class=abstract-for-mobile> <div class="margin-top-30 padding-bottom-30 research-layout is-centered"> <button class="primary orange-text white-bg bigger-text abstract-expand-button-mobile with-border show" style="display: none;"> READ ALL <span class="f1r-icon icon-14_more_small orange vmiddle big"></span> </button> <button class="primary orange-text white-bg bigger-text abstract-expand-button-mobile with-border hide"> READ LESS <span class="f1r-icon icon-10_less_small orange vmiddle big"></span> </button> </div> </div> </div> </div> <div We have addressed all the concerns of the reviewers.&nbsp;These changes have clearly improved our manuscript. We have also included a point-by-point response to the reviewers in addition to making the changes in the manuscript. Our main findings remain unchanged: The final genome comprises 75 327 scaffolds totaling 671 Mb with an N50 of 49 916 kb. The draft assembly is close to the genome size estimated by&nbsp;<i>k</i>-mers distribution and covers 89% of complete and 4.3 % of partial&nbsp;<i>âembryophyta_odb9â lineage orthologous</i>&nbsp;groups in BUSCO. This&nbsp;<i>A. spinosa</i>&nbsp;draft genome will be useful for assessing biodiversity leading to efficient conservation of this endangered endemic tree. Furthermore, the genome may enable genome-assisted cultivar breeding, and provide a better understanding of important metabolic pathways and their underlying genes for both cosmetic and pharmacological purposes. </div> <p class=f1r-article-desk> <a href="https://f1000research.com/articles/7-1310#referee-response-38276" data-path="/reports/38276/responses" class="black-link bold">See the authors' detailed response to the review by Granger Sutton</a><br/> <a href="https://f1000research.com/articles/7-1310#referee-response-38275" data-path="/reports/38275/responses" class="black-link bold">See the authors' detailed response to the review by Amit Sinha</a><br/> </p> <span class=f1r-article-mobile> <div class="margin-top-30 margin-bottom research-layout is-centered" style="display: none;"> <a href="#article-reports"> <button class="primary orange extra-padding">READ REVIEWER RESPONSES</button> </a> </div> </span> </div> <div class=clearfix></div> <div id=article-context class=article-context> <div id=article1-body class=generated-article-body><h2 class=main-title id=d19962e812>Introduction</h2><p class="" id=d19962e815><i>Argania spinosa</i> (L. Skeels) is a tree endemic to the Middle West of Morocco and occupying arid and semi-arid regions totaling up to around 900,000 ha<sup><a href="#ref-1">1</a></sup>. The argane tree forest was recognized as biosphere reserve (Arganeraie Biosphere Reserve) by UNESCO in 1998<sup><a href="#ref-2">2</a></sup>. It is the only unique member of the tropical Sapotaceae family in Morocco<sup><a href="#ref-3">3</a></sup>. In addition to its ecological role in preventing soil erosion and desertification, the argane tree has great cultural and socio-economic importance. The oil extracted from the seed is considered the most expensive edible oil in the world with great cosmetic value and therapeutic potential<sup><a href="#ref-4">4</a>â<a href="#ref-6">6</a></sup>. Argane oil represents a significant source of dietary fatty acids, while the Argane fruit is used as livestock feed by the local population<sup><a href="#ref-7">7</a>â<a href="#ref-9">9</a></sup>. Phytochemical composition of Argane fruits reveals different classes of bioactive compounds, including essential oils, fatty acids, triacylglycerols, flavonoids and their acylglycosyl derivatives, monophenols, phenolic acids, cinnamic acids, saponins, triterpenes, phytosterols, ubiquinone, melatonin, new aminophenols, and vitamin E. Argane oil contains high levels of antioxidant compounds. The long-chain fatty acids in Argane oil are primarily represented by unsaturated oleic acid, then linoleic acid, palmitic acid and stearic acid<sup><a href="#ref-10">10</a></sup>.</p><p class="" id=d19962e851>The distribution area of the Argane forest decreased drastically during the 18th century. Furthermore, about 44 % of the forest was again lost between 1970 and 2007. While there are multiple causes, desertification and overgrazing form the main pressures on the Argane forest<sup><a href="#ref-11">11</a>,<a href="#ref-12">12</a></sup>. Therefore, the management and conservation of the remaining genetic resources of Argane forest are urgent priorities. In recent decades, several studies have been conducted to evaluate the genetic diversity of the Argane tree using morphological<sup><a href="#ref-13">13</a>,<a href="#ref-14">14</a></sup>, chemical<sup><a href="#ref-10">10</a>,<a href="#ref-15">15</a></sup>, biochemical<sup><a href="#ref-6">6</a>,<a href="#ref-16">16</a></sup> and standard molecular marker techniques, all with the aim of describing the genetic diversity of Argane trees and addressing ecological and conservation issues<sup><a href="#ref-17">17</a>â<a href="#ref-25">25</a></sup>. The karyotype of <i>A. spinosa</i> (L.) is constituted of ten pairs of chromosomes (2n =2x =20)<sup><a href="#ref-3">3</a></sup>. Until now, no reference genome was available of the <i>A. spinosa</i> species. Here, we present the Argane tree genome assembled from short and long DNA reads using a hybrid assembly strategy.</p></div><div id=article1-body class=generated-article-body><h2 class=main-title id=d19962e903>Methods and results</h2><div class=section><a name=d19962e906 class=n-a></a><h3 class=section-title>Plant material</h3><p class="" id=d19962e911>The Argane tree (<i>Argania spinosa</i>, taxid 85883, Sapotaceae, family, order Ericales), named <i>Argane AMGHAR</i>, to be sequenced was selected for its biological and ecological characteristics (<a href="#f1">Figure 1</a>). This was a 9-year-old shrub, with weeping form (geotropic, unlike the erect have) with only one main trunk 3 m in height. The ripe fruits has a rounded shape. The plant had semi-evergreen dwarf leaves. The shrub is native to the valley of the plain of Sous, an arid climate with an annual average rainfall of around 220 mm, located between the hills of the Anti-Atlas towards the South East, the Western High Atlas towards the North-West and the Atlantic Ocean towards the West (9Â°32â² 00â³N, 30Â°24â² 00â³W; Altitude: 126 m).</p><a name=f1 class=n-a></a><div class="fig panel clearfix"><a target=_blank href="https://f1000researchdata.s3.amazonaws.com/manuscripts/25962/ef24bf29-a8e4-4f0d-94e2-f36ac2e9030e_figure1.gif"><img alt="ef24bf29-a8e4-4f0d-94e2-f36ac2e9030e_figure1.gif" src="https://f1000researchdata.s3.amazonaws.com/manuscripts/25962/ef24bf29-a8e4-4f0d-94e2-f36ac2e9030e_figure1.gif"></a><div class=caption><h3>Figure 1. Information on the <i>Argania.spinosa</i> individual named #<i>Argane Amghar</i> whose DNA has been sequenced.</h3><p id=d19962e939>(<b>A</b>) Map of Sous region with <i>Argania</i> species distribution. (<b>B</b>) Picture of the tree # <i>Argane Amghar</i>. (Photograph taken by A. El Mousadik).</p></div></div></div><div class=section><a name=d19962e959 class=n-a></a><h3 class=section-title>DNA sequencing and data description</h3><p class="" id=d19962e964>Genomic DNA was extracted from lyophilized leaf tissues of a single tree (<i>Argane AMGHAR</i>) using the Plant DNeasy mini kit (Qiagen, USA). The Argane tree genome was shotgun-sequenced using both Pacbio<sup>TM</sup> (Menlo Park, CA, USA) and Illumina<sup>TM</sup> (San Diego, CA, USA) sequencing technologies, generating 7.6 Gb and 144 Gb of data, respectively. Paired-end libraries with average insert sizes of 600 bp were constructed with Nextera<sup>TM</sup> DNA Library Prep Kit for Illumina (New England BiolabsTM, New Brunswick, MA, USA). These libraries were sequenced on an Illumina HiSeq XTen platform using the PE-150 module and yielded 957,451,810 reads (<a href="#T1">Table 1</a>). These data were trimmed of adapters, yielding a clean set of 936,053,040 reads, representing 236Ã genome coverage, assuming a genome size of 573 Mb as estimated by the <i>k-mer</i> frequency analysis (described below). Raw reads were deposited at the <a target=xrefwindow href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra" id=d19962e985>NCBI Sequence Read Archive</a> (SRA) under accession numbers: <a target=xrefwindow href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra/SRX3207155" id=d19962e988>SRX3207155</a> and <a target=xrefwindow href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra/?term=SRX3207156" id=d19962e991>SRX3207156</a>, corresponding to two independent runs from the same plant DNA sample. In addition, single-molecule long reads from the PacBio RS II platform (Pacific Biosciences, USA) were used to assist the subsequent <i>de novo</i> genome assembly using Illumina. Genomic sequencing libraries were constructed using the PacBio DNA template preparation kit 2.0 (Pacific Biosciences of California, Inc., Menlo Park, CA) for SMRT sequencing on the PacBio RS II machine (Pacific Biosciences of California, Inc.) according to the manufacturerâs instructions, with a size range of 2-15 kb. The constructed libraries were sequenced on six SMRT cells on a PacBio RSII sequencer. The sequences of the 6 SMRT cell runs were deposited at the NCBI SRA under accession numbers: <a target=xrefwindow href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra/?term=SRX1898029" id=d19962e997>SRX1898029</a>/<a target=xrefwindow href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra/?term=SRX1898030" id=d19962e1001>SRX1898030</a>/<a target=xrefwindow href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra/?term=SRX1898031" id=d19962e1004>SRX1898031</a>/<a target=xrefwindow href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra/?term=SRX1898032" id=d19962e1007>SRX1898032</a>/<a target=xrefwindow href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra/?term=SRX1898033" id=d19962e1010>SRX1898033</a>/<a target=xrefwindow href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra/?term=SRX1898034" id=d19962e1013>SRX1898034</a>. The sequencing runs produced about 7.6 Gb, consisting of 6,705,437 reads with an average read length of 2.5 kb and representing about 13Ã genome coverage, again assuming a genome size of 573 Mb (<a href="#T1">Table 1</a>).</p><a name=T1 class=n-a></a><div class="table-wrap panel clearfix"><div class=caption><h3>Table 1. Summary of reads generated from genome sequencing and used in the assembly.</h3></div><table xmlns:ali="http://www.niso.org/schemas/ali/1.0/" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" class=article-table frame=below><a name=d19962e1031 class=n-a></a><thead><a name=d19962e1033 class=n-a></a><tr><a name=d19962e1035 class=n-a></a><th align=left colspan=1 rowspan=2 valign=top><a name=d19962e1037 class=n-a></a>Library<br class=br>technology</th><th align=left colspan=2 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1042 class=n-a></a>Raw data</th><th align=left colspan=2 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1045 class=n-a></a>Trimmed data</th></tr><tr><a name=d19962e1049 class=n-a></a><th align=left colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1051 class=n-a></a>Number of<br class=br>reads</th><th align=left colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1056 class=n-a></a>Number of<br class=br>bases</th><th class=br>bases</th></tr></thead><tbody><a name=d19962e1073 class=n-a></a><tr><a name=d19962e1075 class=n-a></a><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1077 class=n-a></a>Illumina<br class=br>HiSeq X Ten</td><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1082 class=n-a></a>957,451,810</td><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1085 class=n-a></a>144,575,223,310</td><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1088 class=n-a></a>936,053,040</td><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1091 class=n-a></a>135,539,587,270</td></tr><tr><a name=d19962e1095 class=n-a></a><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1097 class=n-a></a>PacBio RS II</td><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1100 class=n-a></a>6,705,437</td><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1103 class=n-a></a>7,649,825,228</td><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1106 class=n-a></a>1,910,887</td><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1109 class=n-a></a>7,078,584,472</td></tr></tbody></table></div></div><div class=section><a name=d19962e1117 class=n-a></a><h3 class=section-title> <i>In silico</i> genome size estimation</h3><p class="" id=d19962e1125>Trimmed reads from the Illumina platform were subjected to <i>k</i>-mer frequency distribution analysis with <a target=xrefwindow href="http://www.cbcb.umd.edu/software/jellyfish/" id=d19962e1130>JELLYFISH</a> v2.1.4 software<sup><a href="#ref-26">26</a>,<a href="#ref-27">27</a></sup>. Analysis parameters were set at -<i>k</i> 21 and 25, and the final result was plotted as a frequency graph (<a href="#f2">Figure 2</a>). Two distinctive modes were observed from the distribution curve: the higher peak at a depth of 44 and reflecting the high heterozygosity of the Argane genome; the lower peak provided a peak depth of 87 for the estimation of the genome size<sup><a href="#ref-28">28</a></sup>. Based on the total number of k-mers obtained, the Argane genome size was calculated to be approximately 573 Mb and 615 Mb, for 21- and 25-mers respectively, using the following formula: total number of k-mer / Peak depth. The double peak of k-mer distribution indicates heterozygosity whose rate is estimated to be 1.58 % and the duplicated fraction of the genome is estimated to be 3,19% (<a href="#f2">Figure 2</a>). The estimated genome size seems to be credible compared to the ones of four other Sapotaceae family members. In fact, according to the <a target=xrefwindow href="http://data.kew.org/cvalues/CvalServlet?generatedby=Angiosperm&amp;querytype=-1&amp;txtEmail=ciufo%40ncbi.nlm.nih.gov&amp;selectfamilytype=phyloFam&amp;chkGenus=on&amp;chkSpecies=on&amp;cmbFourcSelect=0&amp;chkOrigReference=on&amp;cmbPrimeOrAllData=0&amp;txtFamily=sapotaceae&amp;qryfamilytype=phyloFam&amp;txtGenus=&amp;txtSpecies=&amp;txtAuthority=&amp;txtFromFourc=&amp;txtToFourc=&amp;txtFromChromosome=&amp;txtToChromosome=&amp;cmbEstimationMethod=0&amp;txtFromPloidy=&amp;txtToPloidy=&amp;rdoVoucher=2&amp;cmbLifeCycle=0&amp;rdoAngioGroup=3&amp;cmbSort=0" id=d19962e1154>Plant DNA c-values Database</a>, the genome sizes of these four species ranged from 273 Mb in <i>Mimusops elengi</i> L. (c = 0.28 pg) to 2,513 Mb in <i>Isonandra villosa</i> L. (c = 2.57 pg). The other two species are <i>Planchonella eerwah</i> (c = 0.54 pg, 528 Mb) and <i>Madhuca longifolia</i> (c = 0.99 pg, 968 Mb).</p><a name=f2 class=n-a></a><div class="fig panel clearfix"><a target=_blank href="https://f1000researchdata.s3.amazonaws.com/manuscripts/25962/ef24bf29-a8e4-4f0d-94e2-f36ac2e9030e_figure2.gif"><img alt="ef24bf29-a8e4-4f0d-94e2-f36ac2e9030e_figure2.gif" src="https://f1000researchdata.s3.amazonaws.com/manuscripts/25962/ef24bf29-a8e4-4f0d-94e2-f36ac2e9030e_figure2.gif"></a><div class=caption><h3>Figure 2. Distribution of 21 and 25-mers using Jellyfish with PE data Argane whole genome sequencing.</h3></div></div></div><div class=section><a name=d19962e1186 class=n-a></a><h3 class=section-title>Genome assembly and evaluation</h3><p class="" id=d19962e1191>Prior to assembly, Illumina raw reads and PacBio CCS reads were trimmed for adaptor removal using <i>bbduk.sh</i> from BBmap suite (<a target=xrefwindow href="https://github.com/BioInfoTools/BBMap" id=d19962e1196>https://github.com/BioInfoTools/BBMap</a>). Short and long reads were assembled following a hybrid approach using <a target=xrefwindow href="http://www.genome.umd.edu/masurca.html" id=d19962e1199>MaSuRCA assembler</a> v.3.2.2<sup><a href="#ref-29">29</a></sup>. The initial assembly consists of 671,690,540 bp composed of 82,183 contigs with the largest size being 422,848 bp and an N50 of 43,654 bp. The very few contigs (8) with length less than 200 bp were filtered out and the remaining contigs were scaffolded into 75,327 scaffolds totaling 670,096,797 bp; the N50 reached 49,916 bp and the assembly accounted for 2,982,868 Ns with 445.14 Ns per 100 kb (<a href="#T2">Table 2</a>). The scaffolding was done using initial contigs and implemented in MaSuRCA v3.2.4 assembler script using <a target=xrefwindow href="http://wgs-assembler.sourceforge.net/wiki/index.php?title=Main_Page" id=d19962e1210>Celera Assembler</a> v8.3. The GC content was estimated to be 33%. The assembly was screened by <a target=xrefwindow href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/tools/vecscreen/" id=d19962e1213>VecScreen</a> to look for and remove remaining vector contamination. Based on the VecSreen report, contigs containing mitochondrial/chloroplast were also removed. Trimmed PE reads were mapped on the final assembly using <a target=xrefwindow href="https://www.qiagenbioinformatics.com/products/clc-genomics-workbench/" id=d19962e1216>CLC genomics</a> (v11.0, CLCbio, Arhus, Denmark) with 0.8 in length and 0.9 in sequence similarity. In total, 94% of the reads were mapped against the Argane genome. The 6% reads that were unmapped may result from the stringency of mapping criteria used.</p><a name=T2 class=n-a></a><div class="table-wrap panel clearfix"><div class=caption><h3>Table 2. Statistics of the <i>Argania</i> spinosa genome assembly.</h3></div><table xmlns:ali="http://www.niso.org/schemas/ali/1.0/" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" class=article-table frame=below><a name=d19962e1234 class=n-a></a><thead><a name=d19962e1236 class=n-a></a><tr><a name=d19962e1238 class=n-a></a><th colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1240 class=n-a></a></th><th align=left colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1242 class=n-a></a>Number</th><th align=left colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1245 class=n-a></a>Total size (bp)</th><th align=left colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1248 class=n-a></a>N50 (bp)</th><th align=left colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1251 class=n-a></a>Largest (bp)</th></tr></thead><tbody><a name=d19962e1256 class=n-a></a><tr><a name=d19962e1258 class=n-a></a><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1260 class=n-a></a>Contigs</td><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1263 class=n-a></a>82,183</td><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1266 class=n-a></a>671,690,540</td><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1269 class=n-a></a>43,654</td><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1272 class=n-a></a>422,848</td></tr><tr><a name=d19962e1276 class=n-a></a><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1278 class=n-a></a>Scaffolds â¥ 200 bp</td><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1281 class=n-a></a>75,327</td><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1284 class=n-a></a>670,096,797</td><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1287 class=n-a></a>49,916</td><td colspan=1 rowspan=1><a name=d19962e1290 class=n-a></a>422,848</td></tr></tbody></table><div class=table-wrap-foot><div class=footnote><a name=d19962e1298 class=n-a></a><p id=d19962e1300> N50 size defined as the value N such that at least 50% of the genome is covered by scaffolds of size N or larger.</p></div></div></div><p class="" id=d19962e1306>The difference between the genome size estimation and assembly size may be due to the use of parameters excluding extremely high frequency <i>k-</i>mers. They often represent organelle sequences, eventual contaminants inflating the genome size estimation<sup><a href="#ref-30">30</a></sup>, or the high-frequency of repetitive regions found in plant genomes. Furthermore, the genome is highly heterozygous and different allelic regions would inflate assembly size. To assess the completeness of the final assembly, a Benchmarking Universal Single-Copy Orthologs (BUSCO) v3 software approach was used with âembryophyta_odb9â lineage-specific orthologous groups<sup><a href="#ref-31">31</a></sup>. Thus from a total of 1,440 BUSCO genes, 1291 genes (89%) were complete (1179 in single copy and 112 duplicated), 62 genes (4.3%) were represented partially while 87 genes (6%) were missingâ from the assembly.</p></div></div><div id=article1-body class=generated-article-body><h2 class=main-title id=d19962e1324>Conclusions</h2><p class="" id=d19962e1327>This draft genome assembly is a first step towards a global and integrative omics strategy for exhaustive characterization of the Argane tree. In particular, future work will focus on structurally annotating the genome using predictive tools and transcriptome analysis. Other future work will focus on functional gene annotation, finding evidence for genome duplication and comparative genome evolution. A reliable annotation is highly dependent on transcriptomic data, analysis and research. Sequencing of different parts and developmental stages of the Argane transcriptome is ongoing. The metabolome, and analysis of Argane oil biosynthesis, as well as the treeâs microbiome should also be analyzed. To this end, and in order to coordinate the strong interests of the Plant Genomics community for this precious tree, the International Argane Genome Consortium (IAGC) and a resource website has been created (<a target=xrefwindow href="http://www.arganome.org/" id=d19962e1329>www.arganome.org</a>).</p></div><div id=article1-body class=generated-article-body><h2 class=main-title id=d19962e1336>Data availability</h2><p class="" id=d19962e1339>All of the <i>A. spinosa</i> datasets can be retrieved under BioProject accession number <tt>PRJNA294096</tt>: <a target=xrefwindow href="http://identifiers.org/bioproject:PRJNA294096" id=d19962e1347>http://identifiers.org/bioproject:PRJNA294096</a>. The raw reads are available at NCBI Sequence Reads Archive under accession number <tt>SRP077839</tt>: <a target=xrefwindow href="http://identifiers.org/insdc.sra:SRP077839" id=d19962e1353>http://identifiers.org/insdc.sra:SRP077839</a>. The complete genome sequence assembly project has been deposited at GenBank under accession number <tt>QLOD00000000</tt>: <a target=xrefwindow href="http://identifiers.org/ncbigi/GI:1408199612" id=d19962e1360>http://identifiers.org/ncbigi/GI:1408199612</a>. Data can also be retrieved via the International Argane Genome Consortium (IAGC) website: <a target=xrefwindow href="http://www.arganome.org/" id=d19962e1363>http://www.arganome.org</a>.</p></div><div id=article1-body class=generated-article-body><h2 class=main-title id=d19962e1370>Author information</h2><p class="" id=d19962e1373>Slimane Khayi and Nour Elhouda Azza are co-first authors; Rachid Mentag and Hassan Ghazal contributed equally as supervisors.</p></div><div id=article1-back class=generated-article-footer><div class=back-section><a name=d19962e1380 class=n-a></a><h2 class=main-title id=d19962e1382>Acknowledgements</h2><p class="" id=d19962e1385>Thanks are due to the Fulbright Program for supporting Morocco to US exchange PhD students. <div class="popup-window cite-this-article-box research-layout"> <div class="popup-window-title small cite-title">How to cite this report:</div> <span id=cite-report-text-38276-1 data-test-id=mob_report_copy-citation_text> <span class="article-title-and-info in-popup">Sutton G. Reviewer Report For: First draft genome assembly of the Argane tree&nbsp;(<i>Argania spinosa</i>) [version 2; peer review: 2 approved]</span>. <i>F1000Research</i> 2020, <b>7</b>:1310 (<a class=new-orange href="https://doi.org/10.5256/f1000research.17156.r38276" target=_blank>https://doi.org/10.5256/f1000research.17156.r38276</a>) </span> <div class=padding-top data-test-id=report-url> The direct URL for this report is:<br> <a href="https://f1000research.com/articles/7-1310/v1#referee-response-38276" class=new-orange target=_blank>https://f1000research.com/articles/7-1310/v1#referee-response-38276</a> </div> <div class="popup-window-title small note margin-top-20 margin-bottom-20"> <strong>NOTE:</strong> it is important to ensure the information in square brackets after the title is included in this citation. </div> <div class=float-right> <button class="secondary no-fill orange-text-and-border margin-right-20 close-cite-popup uppercase">Close</button> <button class="secondary orange copy-cite-article-version uppercase js-clipboard" title="Copy the current citation details to the clipboard." data-clipboard-target="#cite-report-text-38276-1" data-test-id=mob_report_copy-citation_button>Copy Citation Details</button> </div> </div> </div> </div> </div> </div> <div class="referee-report-info-box referee-report-details-box"> <span class="bold mobile-report-text">Reviewer Report</span>&nbsp;<span class=mobile-report-info>18 Sep 2018</span> </div> <span class="info-separation padding-bottom padding-left"> <div> <span class=bold>Granger Sutton<a href="http://orcid.org/0000-0001-7498-8048" target=_blank title="Open ORCID"><span class=orcid-logo-for-author-list></span></a></span><span class=f1r-article-desk-inline>,</span> J. Craig Venter Institute, 9704 Medical Center Drive, Rockville, MD 20850, USA&nbsp; </div> </span> <div class="research-layout referee-report-status-line"> <span class="f1r-icon icon-86_approved status-green smaller" title=Approved></span> <span class=status-text>Approved</span> </div> <div class=f1r-article-mobile> <span class=article-pubinfo-mobile> <div class="version-info-box views">VIEWS 0</div> </span> </div> <div class=referee-report-content> <div class=hidden-text> <a href="https://doi.org/10.5256/f1000research.17156.r38276" target=_blank>https://doi.org/10.5256/f1000research.17156.r38276</a> </div> <span class=truncated-comment> In the article âFirst draft genome assembly of the Argane tree&nbsp;(<i>Argania spinosa</i>)â, the authors present the draft assembly of the Argane tree using a combination of Illumina and PacBio reads. An argument for the importance of the Argane tree &nbsp;to ... <span class="f1r-article-desk-inline continue-reading-container response-and-comment increment-view-count" data-reportID=38276>Continue reading</span> <div class="f1r-article-mobile research-layout margin-top-30 is-centered"> <button class="primary orange-text white-bg bigger-text expand-button-mobile continue-reading-container show with-border"> READ ALL <span class="f1r-icon icon-14_more_small orange vmiddle big"></span> </button> </div> </span> <span class="hidden hidden-report-text"> <div class=hidden-report-text__comment>In the article âFirst draft genome assembly of the Argane tree&nbsp;(<i>Argania spinosa</i>)â, the authors present the draft assembly of the Argane tree using a combination of Illumina and PacBio reads. An argument for the importance of the Argane tree &nbsp;to the agriculture and economy of the endemic region is given. The assertion that âthe genome may enable genome-assisted cultivar breeding, and provide a better understanding of important metabolic pathways and their underlying genes for both cosmetic and pharmacological purposesâ seems reasonable based on the use of previous genome sequences for important agricultural resources. This article does not claim much beyond providing a reasonable draft genome for <i>A. spinosa</i>. The primary evidence for reasonable quality is three-fold: a k-mer analysis of genome size using Jellyfish, 94% of Illumina reads mapping back to the assembly, and a BUSCO analysis showing 89% full length and 4.3% partial length gene matches for these single copy genes. This is probably sufficient to claim reasonable quality and the usefulness of the genome for downstream research given the contiguity shown by the N50 contig size.<br/> <br/> The authors do miss an opportunity to look more closely at the haplotype separation that may be occurring as they speculate possibly leading to a somewhat larger genome size than indicated by Jellyfish. Iâm not sure why the number of BUSCO genes with more than one full or partial length match was not given â perhaps there were none? The implication that heterozygosity is uniform âThe double peak of&nbsp;<i>k</i>-mer distribution indicates heterozygosity whose rate is estimated to be 1.58%â seems unfounded without more evidence nor is it clear that is the model resulting in this estimate.<br/> <br/> Lastly the grammar would benefit from editing. For example, âA reliable annotation is highly dependent on transcriptomic research, and sequencing of Argane transcriptome analysis of different parts and developmental stages or the plant is ongoing.â Might be better as âA reliable annotation is highly dependent on transcriptomic data, analysis and research. Sequencing of different parts and developmental stages of the Argane transcriptome is ongoing.â.</div> <div class=md> <div class=questionnaire> <ul class=c-questionnaire> <li class=c-questionnaire__item> <p class=c-questionnaire__question>Is the work clearly and accurately presented and does it cite the current literature?</p> <p class=c-questionnaire__answer>Yes</p> </li> <li class=c-questionnaire__item> <p class=c-questionnaire__question>Is the study design appropriate and is the work technically sound?</p> <p class=c-questionnaire__answer>Yes</p> </li> <li class=c-questionnaire__item> <p class=c-questionnaire__question>Are sufficient details of methods and analysis provided to allow replication by others?</p> <p class=c-questionnaire__answer>Yes</p> </li> <li class=c-questionnaire__item> <p class=c-questionnaire__question>If applicable, is the statistical analysis and its interpretation appropriate? </p> <p class=c-questionnaire__answer>Not applicable</p> </li> <li class=c-questionnaire__item> <p class=c-questionnaire__question>Are all the source data underlying the results available to ensure full reproducibility?</p> <p class=c-questionnaire__answer>Yes</p> </li> <li class=c-questionnaire__item> <p class=c-questionnaire__question>Are the conclusions drawn adequately supported by the results?</p> <p class=c-questionnaire__answer>Yes</p> </li> </ul> </div> </div> <p style="margin-top: 10px;"><b class=mobile-block-display>Competing Interests:</b> No competing interests were disclosed.</p> For example, âA reliable annotation is highly dependent on transcriptomic research, and sequencing of Argane transcriptome analysis of different parts and developmental stages or the plant is ongoing.â Might be better as âA reliable annotation is highly dependent on transcriptomic data, analysis and research. Sequencing of different parts and developmental stages of the Argane transcriptome is ongoing.â.&nbsp;<br/> <b>&nbsp;Answer</b>. We agree with the reviewer. The manuscript has been corrected: <ul> <li>&nbsp;&quot;&nbsp;A reliable annotation is highly dependent on transcriptomic research, and sequencing of Argane transcriptome analysis of different parts and developmental stages or the plant is ongoing&quot;&nbsp;has been replaced by &quot; A reliable annotation is highly dependent on transcriptomic data, analysis and research. Sequencing of different parts and developmental stages of the Argane transcriptome is ongoing.â</li> </ul></span> <div class=padding-bottom id=full-comment-5439><b>Answers to Reviewer #2</b><br/> <br/> 1-&nbsp;The authors do miss an opportunity to look more closely at the haplotype separation that may be occurring as they speculate possibly leading to a somewhat larger genome size than indicated by Jellyfish. Iâm not sure why the number of BUSCO genes with more than one full or partial length match was not given â perhaps there were none? The implication that heterozygosity is uniform âThe double peak of&nbsp;k-mer distribution indicates heterozygosity whose rate is estimated to be 1.58%â seems unfounded without more evidence nor is it clear that is the model resulting in this estimate.&nbsp;<br/> <b>Answer</b>. We agree with the reviewer. The manuscript has been corrected: <ul> <li>â..which showed that the assembly contained 89% (1271 genes) of complete and 4.3% (62 genes) of partial sequences that were Arabidopsis orthologs.â has been replaced by â. Thus, from a total of 1,440 BUSCO genes, 1291 genes (89%) were complete (1179 in single copy and 112 duplicated), 62 genes (4.3%) were represented partially while 87 genes (6%) were missingâ from the assembly.</li> </ul> 2- Lastly the grammar would benefit from editing. For example, âA reliable annotation is highly dependent on transcriptomic research, and sequencing of Argane transcriptome analysis of different parts and developmental stages or the plant is ongoing.â Might be better as âA reliable annotation is highly dependent on transcriptomic data, analysis and research. Sequencing of different parts and developmental stages of the Argane transcriptome is ongoing.â.&nbsp;<br/> <b>&nbsp;Answer</b>. We agree with the reviewer. The manuscript has been corrected: <ul> <li>&nbsp;&quot;&nbsp;A reliable annotation is highly dependent on transcriptomic research, and sequencing of Argane transcriptome analysis of different parts and developmental stages or the plant is ongoing&quot;&nbsp;has been replaced by &quot; A reliable annotation is highly dependent on transcriptomic data, analysis and research. Sequencing of different parts and developmental stages of the Argane transcriptome is ongoing.â</li> </ul></div> <span class="disclosures competing-interests-display padding-top"> <strong>Competing class="comment-wrapper not-sortable button-wrapper"> <div class=comment-button-wrapper> <a href="/login?originalPath=/articles/7-1310/v2&scrollTo=referee-response-38276" data-test-id=cite-report-2>Cite</a> </div> <div id=cite-report-popup-38275-2 class="popup-window-wrapper is-hidden"> <div class=cite-popup-background></div> <div class="popup-window cite-this-article-box research-layout"> <div class="popup-window-title small cite-title">How to cite this report:</div> <span id=cite-report-text-38275-2 data-test-id=mob_report_copy-citation_text> <span class="article-title-and-info in-popup">Sinha A. Reviewer Report For: First draft genome assembly of the Argane tree&nbsp;(<i>Argania spinosa</i>) [version 2; peer review: 2 approved]</span>. <i>F1000Research</i> 2020, <b>7</b>:1310 (<a class=new-orange href="https://doi.org/10.5256/f1000research.17156.r38275" target=_blank>https://doi.org/10.5256/f1000research.17156.r38275</a>) </span> <div class=padding-top data-test-id=report-url> The direct URL for this report is:<br> <a href="https://f1000research.com/articles/7-1310/v1#referee-response-38275" class=new-orange target=_blank>https://f1000research.com/articles/7-1310/v1#referee-response-38275</a> </div> <div class="popup-window-title small note margin-top-20 margin-bottom-20"> <strong>NOTE:</strong> it is important to ensure the information in square brackets after the title is included in this citation. </div> <div class=float-right> <button class="secondary no-fill orange-text-and-border margin-right-20 close-cite-popup uppercase">Close</button> <button class="secondary orange copy-cite-article-version uppercase js-clipboard" title="Copy the current citation details to the clipboard." data-clipboard-target="#cite-report-text-38275-2" data-test-id=mob_report_copy-citation_button>Copy Citation Details</button> </div> </div> </div> </div> </div> </div> <div class="referee-report-info-box referee-report-details-box"> <span class="bold mobile-report-text">Reviewer Report</span>&nbsp;<span class=mobile-report-info>17 Sep 2018</span> </div> <span class="info-separation padding-bottom padding-left"> <div> <span class=bold>Amit Sinha<a href="http://orcid.org/0000-0003-1849-710X" target=_blank title="Open ORCID"><span class=orcid-logo-for-author-list></span></a></span><span class=f1r-article-desk-inline>,</span> New England Biolabs Inc., Ipswich, MA, USA&nbsp; </div> </span> <div class="research-layout referee-report-status-line"> <span class="f1r-icon icon-87_approved_reservations status-green smaller" title="Approved with Reservations"></span> <span class=status-text>Approved with Reservations</span> </div> <div class=f1r-article-mobile> <span class=article-pubinfo-mobile> <div class="version-info-box views">VIEWS 0</div> </span> </div> <div class=referee-report-content> <div class=hidden-text> <a href="https://doi.org/10.5256/f1000research.17156.r38275" target=_blank>https://doi.org/10.5256/f1000research.17156.r38275</a> </div> <span class=truncated-comment> In the current manuscript, the authors present the first draft genome assembly for the argan tree <i>Argania spinosa</i>, a tree with significant ecological as well as commercial importance.<br/> The authors have used a hybrid assembly approach, combing data from ... <span class="f1r-article-desk-inline continue-reading-container response-and-comment increment-view-count" data-reportID=38275>Continue reading</span> <div class="f1r-article-mobile research-layout margin-top-30 is-centered"> <button class="primary orange-text white-bg bigger-text expand-button-mobile continue-reading-container show with-border"> READ ALL <span class="f1r-icon icon-14_more_small orange vmiddle big"></span> </button> </div> </span> <span class="hidden hidden-report-text"> <div class=hidden-report-text__comment>In the current manuscript, the authors present the first draft genome assembly for the argan tree <i>Argania spinosa</i>, a tree with significant ecological as well as commercial importance.<br/> The authors have used a hybrid assembly approach, combing data from both Illumina short-reads and PacBio long-reads technology. Use of such hybrid approaches is welcome, as they can combine the&nbsp; advantages offered by different technological platforms.<br/> Based on a k-mer analysis, the authors also provide a reasonable estimate of the genome-size and the level of heterozygosity. These are important metrics to report, as they can guide the methods to be used for genome assembly, as well as for interpretation of the assembled genome sequence. The draft genome has been satisfactorily assembled, using state of the art computational methods, and it contains 89% of the predicted core genes as defined in the BUSCO software.<br/> <br/> It is hoped that in their future studies, the authors will follow up with more improvements to the draft genome, including gene annotations using transcriptomic data.<br/> <br/> Overall, manuscript provides valuable information and sequence resources that will be useful to the scientific community.&nbsp; I have only 1 major and 6 minor comments/suggestions that I think the authors should be able to address.<br/> <br/> <b>Major reservation:</b><br/> <br/> 1. Both Illumina as well as PacBio reads have been processed and trimmed before being used as an input to the MaSuRCA software. However, the instructions for the MaSuRCA software explicitly ask for <u><b>NOT</b></u> using any third-party tools, or performing any trimming, cleaning or error correction on Illumina reads, as it will most likely lead to a deteriorated assembly&nbsp; (See https://github.com/alekseyzimin/masurca#overview). It is therefore strongly suggested that the authors try an assembly with the raw Illumina reads directly, as it might lead to a better assembly. If such an analysis was already performed but the assembly was worse than the current version, please provide this information in the manuscript.<br/> <br/> <b>Minor comment/suggestion:</b><br/> <br/> 1. For PacBio data, please specify the form of processed reads that were input to the MaSuRCA software: were they the raw PacBio reads, or the Circular Consensus Sequence&nbsp; (CCS) reads?<br/> <br/> 2. The authors report that the genomic DNA was size-selected for fragments above 2kb. What was the approximate maximum size of input DNA for PacBio library preparation. Also, what was the maximum size of PacBio reads (e.g after the CCS step) ?<br/> <br/> 3. The raw coverage obtained from Illumina data is reported as 160X. But as per my calculations, based on number of trimmed bases in table 1 and a estimated genome size of 573 Mb, I obtain 135,539,587,270 / 573,000,000 =&nbsp; 236X. Please correct or explain further.<br/> <br/> 4. In addition to the observed heterozygosity, the repeat content of the genome could be an important reason for a fragmented assembly. The k-mer analysis can also be used to estimate the % of genome that is comprised of repeats. It will be great if this estimate is provided.<br/> <br/> 5. For the BUSCO analysis, the authors report using the Arabidopsis lineage-specific orthologous groups. However, from the BUSCO manual, the only valid value for the lineage parameter seems to be âembryophyta_odb9â, which internally uses Arabidopsis hmms for Augustus-based gene predictions, but the member proteins are form multiple species. If this is the lineage parameter the authors used, please specifiy it as âembryophyta_odb9â rather than Arabidopsis, or provide more details on how the Arabidopsis BUSCO groups were determined.<br/> <br/> 6. The genome sequences of the organelles mitochondria and chloroplast are also very important in investigating the biology of any species, and also serve as important resource for evolutionary and phylogenetic studies. Therefore, it will be great if instead of completely&nbsp;removing the organellar genomes, the authors provide them as separate set of sequences, in separate files and ideally as separate GenBank entries.</div> <div class=md> <div class=questionnaire> <ul class=c-questionnaire> <li class=c-questionnaire__item> <p class=c-questionnaire__question>Is the work clearly and accurately presented and does it cite the current literature?</p> <p class=c-questionnaire__answer>Yes</p> </li> <li class=c-questionnaire__item> <p class=c-questionnaire__question>Is the study design appropriate and is the work technically sound?</p> <p class=c-questionnaire__answer>Yes</p> </li> <li class=c-questionnaire__item> <p class=c-questionnaire__question>Are sufficient details of methods and analysis provided to allow replication by others?</p> <p class=c-questionnaire__answer>Yes</p> </li> <li class=c-questionnaire__item> <p class=c-questionnaire__question>If applicable, is the statistical analysis and its interpretation appropriate? </p> <p class=c-questionnaire__answer>Yes</p> </li> <li class=c-questionnaire__item> <p class=c-questionnaire__question>Are all the source data underlying the results available to ensure full reproducibility?</p> <p class=c-questionnaire__answer>Yes</p> </li> <li class=c-questionnaire__item> <p class=c-questionnaire__question>Are the conclusions drawn adequately supported by the results?</p> <p class=c-questionnaire__answer>Yes</p> </li> </ul> </div> </div> <p style="margin-top: 10px;"><b class=mobile-block-display>Competing Interests:</b> No competing interests were disclosed.</p> <span class="info-separation padding-top padding-bottom comment-statement-mobile"> <div class=f1r-article-mobile> <div class="content-divider report-info"></div> </div> <strong> I confirm that I have read this submission and believe that I have an appropriate level of expertise to confirm that it is of an acceptable scientific standard, however I have significant reservations, as outlined above. </strong> </span> <div class=f1r-article-mobile> <div class="content-divider report-info"></div> </div> <span class="f1r-article-desk hide-comment-container However, the instructions for the MaSuRCA software explicitly ask for&nbsp;<b><u>NOT</u></b>&nbsp;using any third-party tools, or performing any trimming, cleaning or error correction on Illumina reads, as it will most likely lead to a deteriorated assembly&nbsp; (See https://github.com/alekseyzimin/masurca#overview). Therefore, it will be great if instead of completely&nbsp;removing the organellar genomes, the authors provide them as separate set of sequences, in separate files and ideally as separate GenBank entries.&nbsp;<br/> <br/> <b>Response:</b><br/> We agree with the reviewer. The work is in progress and we plant to publish the organellar genomes soon in a separate manuscript.</div> <span class="disclosures competing-interests-display padding-top"> <strong>Competing Interests:</strong> <span class=c-i-d>The authors declare No conflict interests with this peer review.</span> </span> <span class="hide-comment-container response-and-comment">Close</span> </span> <div class=report-concern-wrapper> <a href="mailto:research@f1000.com?subject=Report a concern (15719) " class=report-a-concern-link>Report a concern</a> </div> </div> </div> </li> <li class="comment-wrapper not-sortable response-on-mobile" data-commentID=5438> <div class="one-comment with-divider "> <a name=article-comment-5438></a> <div class="f1r-article-desk commenter-role"> Author Response 04 May 2020 </div> <div> <span class=name>Rachid Mentag</span><span class=name>, </span><span class=commenter-affiliation>National Institute of Agricultural Research (INRA), Rabat, Morocco</span> </div> <div class="f1r-article-mobile the-comment-date"> 04 May 2020 </div> <div class=f1r-article-mobile> <div class="article-pubinfo-mobile comments-section"> <span class="version-info-box comments"> Author Response </span> </div> </div> <div class="comment-content "> <span class=truncated-comment> <b>Answers to Reviewer #1</b><br/> &nbsp;<br/> <b>Major reservation:</b><br/> &nbsp;<br/> 1.&nbsp;Both Illumina as well as PacBio reads have been processed and trimmed before being used as an input to the MaSuRCA software. ... <span class="continue-reading-container response-and-comment">Continue reading</span> </span> <span class="full-comment hidden"> <span id=full-comment-original-5438 class=hidden><b>Answers to Reviewer #1</b><br/> &nbsp;<br/> <b>Major reservation:</b><br/> &nbsp;<br/> 1.&nbsp;Both Illumina as well as PacBio reads have been processed and trimmed before being used as an input to the MaSuRCA software. However, the instructions for the MaSuRCA software explicitly ask for&nbsp;<b><u>NOT</u></b>&nbsp;using any third-party tools, or performing any trimming, cleaning or error correction on Illumina reads, as it will most likely lead to a deteriorated assembly&nbsp; (See https://github.com/alekseyzimin/masurca#overview). It is therefore strongly suggested that the authors try an assembly with the raw Illumina reads directly, as it might lead to a better assembly. If such an analysis was already performed but the assembly was worse than the current version, please provide this information in the manuscript.<br/> <b>Answer.</b>We agree with the reviewer. Both illumina and PacBio reads have been trimmed only for adaptor removal. No quality trimming was performed. The manuscript has been corrected:<br/> &nbsp; <ul> <li>âQuality-filtered reads from the Illuminaâ has been replaced by âTrimmed reads from the Illuminaâ</li> <li>âThese data was trimmed of adapters and low-quality sequences,â¦â has been replaced by âThese data was trimmed of adapters,â¦â</li> <li>âPrior to assembly, Illumina and PacBio raw reads were trimmed for quality and adaptor removal using bbduk.shâ has beenreplaced by âPrior to assembly, Illumina raw reads and PacBio CCS reads were trimmed for adaptor removal using bbduk.shâ&nbsp;</li> </ul> <b>Minor comment/suggestion:</b><br/> <br/> 1-&nbsp;For PacBio data, please specify the form of processed reads that were input to the MaSuRCA software: were they the raw PacBio reads, or the Circular Consensus Sequence&nbsp; (CCS) reads?&nbsp;<br/> <b>Answer</b>. CCS PacBio reads were processed within MaSuRCA software. The manuscript has been corrected:<br/> &nbsp; <ul> <li>âPrior to assembly,&nbsp;Short and long reads wereâ¦â has been replaced by âPrior to assembly, Illumina raw reads and PacBio CCS reads were&nbsp;â¦â</li> </ul> <br/> 2-&nbsp;The authors report that the genomic DNA was size-selected for fragments above 2kb. What was the approximate maximum size of input DNA for PacBio library preparation. Also, what was the maximum size of PacBio reads (e.g after the CCS step) ?&nbsp;<br/> <b>Answer</b>.DNA extracted from the lyophilized leaves was divided into HMW and LMW fractions, and each was used separately to make PacBio libraries. The best PacBio SMRT cell yielded 4G of data on 163,000 spots, with an average read size of 24,468 bases.<br/> &nbsp;<br/> 3- The raw coverage obtained from Illumina data is reported as 160X. But as per my calculations, based on number of trimmed bases in table 1 and a estimated genome size of 573 Mb, I obtain 135,539,587,270 / 573,000,000 =&nbsp;236X. Please correct or explain further.&nbsp;<br/> <b>Answer</b>.We agree with the reviewer. The manuscript have been corrected:<br/> &nbsp; <ul> <li>ââ¦.yielding a clean set of 936,053,040 reads, representing 160&times; genome coverage,â has now been replaced by ââ¦yielding a clean set of 936,053,040 reads, representing 236x genome coverage,â</li> </ul> &nbsp;<br/> 4- In addition to the observed heterozygosity, the repeat content of the genome could be an important reason for a fragmented assembly. The k-mer analysis can also be used to estimate the % of genome that is comprised of repeats. It will be great if this estimate is provided.&nbsp;<br/> <b>Answer</b>.Based on the 21-mer distribution analysis, the duplicated fraction of the genome is estimated to be 3,19%. The revised version of the manuscript has been corrected:<br/> &nbsp; <ul> <li>âThe double peak of k-mer distribution indicates heterozygosity whose rate is estimated to be 1.58 % (<a href="https://f1000research.com/articles/7-1310/v1#f2">Figure 2</a>).â Has been replaced by âThe double peak of k-mer distribution indicates heterozygosity whose rate is estimated to be 1.58 % and the duplicated fraction of the genome is estimated to be 3,19% (<a href="https://f1000research.com/articles/7-1310/v1#f2">Figure 2</a>).â</li> </ul> &nbsp;<br/> 5- For the BUSCO analysis, the authors report using the Arabidopsis lineage-specific orthologous groups. However, from the BUSCO manual, the only valid value for the lineage parameter seems to be âembryophyta_odb9â, which internally uses Arabidopsis hmms for Augustus-based gene predictions, but the member proteins are form multiple species. If this is the lineage parameter the authors used, please specifiy it as âembryophyta_odb9â rather than Arabidopsis, or provide more details on how the Arabidopsis BUSCO groups were determined.&nbsp;<br/> <b>Answer</b>. We agree with the reviewer. The lineage parameter used was âembryophyta_odb9â. The manuscript has been corrected:<br/> &nbsp; <ul> <li>âTo assess the completeness of the final assembly, a&nbsp;<a href="https://busco.ezlab.org/">Benchmarking Universal Single-Copy Orthologs</a>&nbsp;(BUSCO) v3 software approach was used with Arabidopsis lineage-specific orthologous groups...â has been replaced by âTo assess the completeness of the final assembly, a&nbsp;<a href="https://busco.ezlab.org/">Benchmarking Universal Single-Copy Orthologs</a>&nbsp;(BUSCO) v3 software approach was used with âembryophyta_odb9â lineage-specific orthologous groups...â</li> </ul> &nbsp;<br/> 6- The genome sequences of the organelles mitochondria and chloroplast are also very important in investigating the biology of any species, and also serve as important resource for evolutionary and phylogenetic studies. Therefore, it will be great if instead of completely&nbsp;removing the organellar genomes, the authors provide them as separate set of sequences, in separate files and ideally as separate GenBank entries.&nbsp;<br/> <b>Answer</b>.We agree with the reviewer. The work is in progress and we plan to publish the organellar genomes soon in separate manuscripts.</span> <div class=padding-bottom id=full-comment-5438><b>Answers to Reviewer #1</b><br/> &nbsp;<br/> <b>Major reservation:</b><br/> &nbsp;<br/> 1.&nbsp;Both Illumina as well as PacBio reads have been processed and trimmed before being used as an input to the MaSuRCA software. u-black--high"><span class="u-ib u-middle"> <i class="c-icn--f1r-icon c-icn--approved " title=Approved #data-refInfo=""></i> </span> <span class="u-middle u-ib u-ml--1/2">Approved</span></dt> <dd class="c-definitions__description t-caption">The paper is scientifically sound in its current form and only minor, if any, improvements are suggested</dd> <dt class="c-definitions__term u-upper t-control u-weight--md u-black--high"><span class="u-ib u-middle"> <i class="c-icn--f1r-icon c-icn--reservations" title="Approved with Reservations" #data-refInfo=""></i> </span> <span class="u-middle u-ib u-ml--1/2">Approved with reservations</span></dt> <dd class="c-definitions__description t-caption"> A number of small changes, sometimes more significant revisions are required to address specific details and improve the papers academic merit. </dd> <dt class="c-definitions__term u-upper t-control u-weight--md u-black--high"><span class="u-ib u-middle"> <i class="c-icn--f1r-icon c-icn--not-approved " title="Not Approved" #data-refInfo=""></i> </span> <span class="u-middle u-ib u-ml--1/2">Not approved</span></dt> <dd class="c-definitions__description t-caption">Fundamental flaws in the paper seriously undermine the findings and conclusions</dd> </dl> </div> </div> </div> </div> <div class="">In the article âFirst draft genome assembly of the Argane tree&nbsp;(<i>Argania spinosa</i>)â, the authors present the draft assembly of the Argane tree using a combination of Illumina and PacBio reads. An argument for the importance of the Argane tree &nbsp;to the agriculture and economy of the endemic region is given. The assertion that âthe genome may enable genome-assisted cultivar breeding, and provide a better understanding of important metabolic pathways and their underlying genes for both cosmetic and pharmacological purposesâ seems reasonable based on the use of previous genome sequences for important agricultural resources. This article does not claim much beyond providing a reasonable draft genome for <i>A. spinosa</i>. The primary evidence for reasonable quality is three-fold: a k-mer analysis of genome size using Jellyfish, 94% of Illumina reads mapping back to the assembly, and a BUSCO analysis showing 89% full length and 4.3% partial length gene matches for these single copy genes. This is probably sufficient to claim reasonable quality and the usefulness of the genome for downstream research given the contiguity shown by the N50 contig size.<br/> <br/> The authors do miss an opportunity to look more closely at the haplotype separation that may be occurring as they speculate possibly leading to a somewhat larger genome size than indicated by Jellyfish. Iâm not sure why the number of BUSCO genes with more than one full or partial length match was not given â perhaps there were none? The implication that heterozygosity is uniform âThe double peak of&nbsp;<i>k</i>-mer distribution indicates heterozygosity whose rate is estimated to be 1.58%â seems unfounded without more evidence nor is it clear that is the model resulting in this estimate.<br/> <br/> Lastly the grammar would benefit from editing. For example, âA reliable annotation is highly dependent on transcriptomic research, and sequencing of Argane transcriptome analysis of different parts and developmental stages or the plant is ongoing.â Might be better as âA reliable annotation is highly dependent on transcriptomic data, analysis and research. Sequencing of different parts and developmental stages of the Argane transcriptome is ongoing.â.</div> <div class=u-mb--2> <div class=md> <div class=questionnaire> <ul class=c-questionnaire> <li class=c-questionnaire__item> <p class=c-questionnaire__question>Is the work clearly and accurately presented and does it cite the current literature?</p> <p class=c-questionnaire__answer>Yes</p> </li> <li class=c-questionnaire__item> <p class=c-questionnaire__question>Is the study design appropriate and is the work technically sound?</p> <p class=c-questionnaire__answer>Yes</p> </li> <li class=c-questionnaire__item> <p class=c-questionnaire__question>Are sufficient details of methods and analysis provided to allow replication by others?</p> <p class=c-questionnaire__answer>Yes</p> </li> <li class=c-questionnaire__item> <p class=c-questionnaire__question>If applicable, is the statistical analysis and its interpretation appropriate? </p> <p class=c-questionnaire__answer>Not applicable</p> </li> <li class=c-questionnaire__item> <p class=c-questionnaire__question>Are all the source data underlying the results available to ensure full reproducibility?</p> <p class=c-questionnaire__answer>Yes</p> </li> <li class=c-questionnaire__item> <p class=c-questionnaire__question>Are the conclusions drawn adequately supported by the results?</p> <p class=c-questionnaire__answer>Yes</p> </li> </ul> </div> </div> </div> <hr class="c-hr c-hr--low u-mb--2"> <h5 class="t-body u-weight--md u-mt--0 u-mb--1/2">Competing Interests</h5> <p class="u-mt--0 u-mb--2 u-italic">No competing interests were disclosed.</p> <hr class="c-hr c-hr--low u-mb--2"> <h5 class="t-body u-weight--md u-mt--0 u-mb--1/2">Reviewer Expertise</h5> <p class="u-mb--2 u-mt--0">Whole genome shotgun assembly, pan-genome analysis</p> <hr class="c-hr c-hr--low u-mb--3"> <p class="u-mb--3 u-mt--0"> <strong> I confirm that I have read this submission and believe that I have an appropriate level of expertise to confirm that it is of an acceptable scientific standard. </strong> </p> <div class="_mdl-layout u-mb--3"> <a href="/login?originalPath=/articles/7-1310/v2&scrollTo=referee-response-38276" class="u-1/1 mdl-button mdl-js-button mdl-button--outline mdl-button--multi-line mdl-button--colored mdl-button--white-ish" data-test-id=article_referee-report_respond><i class="material-icons u-ib u-middle">reply</i><span class="p-article__sidebar-report-respond-text u-ib u-middle">Respond to this report</span></a> </div> <hr class="c-hr c-hr--low c-hr--md u-mb--3"> <section id=report-responses-38276> <h4 class="t-h3 u-weight--md u-mb--2 u-mt--0">Responses <span class="u-weight--rg u-black--medium t-body">(1)</span></h4> <span class="c-hr c-hr--low u-mb--3"></span> <article id=referee-report-comment-5439 class="c-comment js-referee-report-comment " data-commentid=5439 data-reportid=38276 data-test-id=article_referee_report_comment> <header> <div class="c-comment__role t-caption u-black--medium" data-test-id=article_referee-report-comment_roles> <span Agricultural Research (INRA), Rabat, Morocco</span> </h5> <div class="c-comment__body u-mb--1"> <div class="c-read-more js-read-more t-body" data-lines=4> <div class="c-read-more__content js-read-more-content "> <div class=u-mb--1 data-test-id=article_referee-report-comment_text data-commentid=5439><b>Answers to Reviewer #2</b><br/> <br/> 1-&nbsp;The authors do miss an opportunity to look more closely at the haplotype separation that may be occurring as they speculate possibly leading to a somewhat larger genome size than indicated by Jellyfish. Iâm not sure why the number of BUSCO genes with more than one full or partial length match was not given â perhaps there were none? The implication that heterozygosity is uniform âThe double peak of&nbsp;k-mer distribution indicates heterozygosity whose rate is estimated to be 1.58%â seems unfounded without more evidence nor is it clear that is the model resulting in this estimate.&nbsp;<br/> <b>Answer</b>. We agree with the reviewer. The manuscript has been corrected: <ul> <li>â..which showed that the assembly contained 89% (1271 genes) of complete and 4.3% (62 genes) of partial sequences that were Arabidopsis orthologs.â has been replaced by â. Thus, from a total of 1,440 BUSCO genes, 1291 genes (89%) were complete (1179 in single copy and 112 duplicated), 62 genes (4.3%) were represented partially while 87 genes (6%) were missingâ from the assembly.</li> </ul> 2- Lastly the grammar would benefit from editing. For example, âA reliable annotation is highly dependent on transcriptomic research, and sequencing of Argane transcriptome analysis of different parts and developmental stages or the plant is ongoing.â Might be better as âA reliable annotation is highly dependent on transcriptomic data, analysis and research. Sequencing of different parts and developmental stages of the Argane transcriptome is ongoing.â.&nbsp;<br/> <b>&nbsp;Answer</b>. We agree with the reviewer. The manuscript has been corrected: <ul> <li>&nbsp;&quot;&nbsp;A reliable annotation is highly dependent on transcriptomic research, and sequencing of Argane transcriptome analysis of different parts and developmental stages or the plant is ongoing&quot;&nbsp;has been replaced by &quot; A reliable annotation is highly dependent on transcriptomic data, analysis and research. Sequencing of different parts and developmental stages of the Argane transcriptome is ongoing.â</li> </ul></div> </div> <a href="#" class="c-read-more__toggle js-read-more-toggle t-caption"> <span class=c-read-more__expand>View more</span> <span class=c-read-more__contract>View less</span> </a> </div> </div> <div class=c-comment__footer> <h5 class="t-body u-weight--md u-mt--0 u-mb--1/2">Competing Interests</h5> <p class="u-mt--0 u-mb--1 u-italic" data-test-id=article_referee-report-comment_competing-interests>No competing interests were disclosed.</p> </div> <footer> <div class="o-actions o-actions--middle"> <div class=o-actions__primary> <a href="/login?originalPath=/articles/7-1310/v2&scrollTo=referee-response-38276" class="js-referee-report-comment c-link--basic" data-test-id=article_referee-report-comment_respond><i class="material-icons c-link__icon">reply</i> <span class=c-link__text>Respond</span></a> </div> <div class=o-actions__secondary> <a href="mailto:research@f1000.com?subject=Report a concern (15719) " data-test-id=article_referee-report-comment_concern class="js-report-concern t-caption c-link c-link--inline">Report a concern</a> </div> </div> </footer> </header> </article> </section> <script type="text/template" data-template=refereeReportCitation-38276 id=refereeReportCitation-38276 class=u-hide>
